Unexpectedly, Pan Lai Defeats Crawford

| Wins the All-American Singles Championship |

French and Wimbledon Champion

Defeated by British Davis Cup Player

(New York, Forest Hills, 10th, Reuters) The result of the All-American Tennis Open singles final was quite unexpected. British Davis Cup player Pan Lai defeated Australian Crawford, the French and Wimbledon champion, in five sets. The scores are as follows:

6-3

11-13

Pan Lai 4-6 Crawford

6-0

6-1

Wins First Set First Although Pan Lai's victory was unexpected, it was certainly deserved. In the first set, he used powerful groundstrokes to attack the corners, then came to the net to finish.

Lost Twice in a Row In the second set, Pan Lai took a 3-1 lead, but Crawford fought back to win it. Crawford then won the third set, with his magnificent backhand strokes earning him many points.

Final Victory In the last two sets, Pan Lai completely controlled his opponent, losing only one game in both sets. Pan Lai's serve was fierce and frightening, while Crawford seemed helpless.

Knee Injury Affects The wind was very strong, causing many double faults for both sides. It should also be noted that Crawford injured his knee when he fell during his semi-final victory over Shields. The extent of the impact is difficult to say.

Li Huitang Suffering from Pneumonia

(Batavia Correspondence) Mr. Li Huitang fell ill at the beginning of this month. The president of the Chinese Qunli Sports Association, Mr. Zhong Wensheng, introduced him to Dr. Fu Lan's clinic for diagnosis on August 22nd. According to Dr. Wang, Mr. Li is suffering from pleurisy and was instructed to return for further diagnosis at 8:00 AM on the 23rd, including an X-ray examination. The X-ray confirmed the diagnosis of pleurisy, requiring hospitalization for rest. Therefore, that afternoon, Mr. Li was admitted to the Yansheng Hospital. On the 24th, Dr. Wang told Mr. Li that the X-ray showed that his lungs and heart were fine, but there was fluid in the pleura. With hospitalization and rest, he could recover in a month or a month and a half. Mr. Li, having read in a certain Chinese newspaper that he had a lung injury, feared that his relatives and friends would worry. Several friends visited him at the hospital to inquire about his condition. He explained the condition in detail and especially conveyed the findings of Dr. Wang's examination to the newspaper, in order to allay the concerns of his relatives and friends.

The Municipal Education Bureau Announces the Competition Regulations for the City Games

Tennis Divided into Singles and Doubles

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, in preparation for selecting athletes to attend the National Games on Double Ten Day, is organizing the Third City Games, to be held from the 21st to the 23rd of this month at the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation stadium on Route Labor Father. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. Regarding the tennis registration announced yesterday by the Tennis Committee, only singles were mentioned. It is now known that both singles and doubles will be held simultaneously. It is hoped that Shanghai tennis players will register to participate. The Municipal Education Bureau announced the competition regulations for this year's games as follows:

Competition Regulations

Article 1: Date and Location

The games will be held from September 21st to 23rd, 1933, at the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation stadium. However, swimming and ball games may be held earlier.

Article 2: Participating Athletes

(1) Any citizen currently residing in this city, male aged 18 or older, female aged 16 or older, in good health, of good character, and not violating the rules and spirit of amateur sports, may participate.

(2) Individuals may participate in track and field, pentathlon, decathlon, swimming, and tennis.

(3) Teams may participate in soccer, basketball, volleyball, and softball.

Article 3: Championship Categories

The championship categories for this competition are as follows:

(1) Men's Division: Track and Field Championship, Running Championship, Pentathlon Championship, Decathlon Championship, Swimming Championship, Soccer Championship, Basketball Championship, Tennis Championship, Volleyball Championship, Baseball Championship.

(2) Women's Division: Track and Field Championship, Swimming Championship, Basketball Championship, Tennis Championship, Volleyball Championship, Softball Championship.

(3) National Arts Division: Boxing Championship, Wrestling Championship, Weapons (Spear, Saber, Sword, Staff) Championship, Archery Championship, Pellet Shooting Championship, Shuttlecock Kicking Championship, Strength Test Championship.

Article 4: Sports Events

The sports events included in the Track and Field, Pentathlon, Decathlon, and Swimming Championships are as follows:

(1) Track and Field: (A) Men's Track and Field: High Jump, Pole Vault, Long Jump, Triple Jump, Shot Put (16 lbs), Discus Throw, Javelin Throw. (B) Men's Running: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1500 meters, 10,000 meters, 110-meter Hurdles, 400-meter Hurdles. (C) Women's Track and Field: High Jump, Long Jump, Javelin Throw, Shot Put, 100 meters, 80-meter Hurdles.

(2) Pentathlon and Decathlon: (A) Pentathlon: Long Jump, Javelin Throw, 200 meters, Discus Throw, 1500 meters.

(B) Decathlon: 100 meters, Long Jump, Shot Put (16 lbs), High Jump, 400 meters, 110-meter Hurdles, Discus Throw, Pole Vault, Javelin Throw, 1500 meters.

(3) Swimming: (A) Men's: 50-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Backstroke, 200-meter Breaststroke, 400-meter Freestyle, 1500-meter Freestyle, 200-meter Relay, Diving Competition. (B) Women's: 50-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Freestyle, 100-meter Backstroke, 200-meter Breaststroke.

Article 5: Athletes' Participation and Championship Winning Methods

(1) Each male or female athlete may not participate in more than four track and field or swimming events. Each national arts athlete may not participate in more than two events.

(2) No athlete may participate in both the pentathlon and decathlon.

(3) In each track and field, pentathlon, decathlon, swimming, and national arts event, the top four finishers will be recorded.

(4) Points for each swimming, national arts, and track and field event will be calculated as 5, 3, 2, 1. Points for the pentathlon and decathlon will be calculated as 10, 6, 4, 2.

(5) The athlete with the highest total score will win the championship. If two or more athletes have the same score, the athlete with the most first-place finishes will be the winner. If the number of first-place finishes is also the same, then the number of second-place finishes will be used, and so on.

(6) The competition rules will follow the rules for men's and women's track and field competitions as reviewed and approved by the National Games of 1933 and the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation.

Article 6: Soccer Championship

(1) Each team is limited to 15 registered players.

(2) The competition will use an elimination system. The order will be drawn by the competition department. The winner of the final will win the championship.

(3) If two teams are tied, the time should be extended to resolve the tie. If the tie cannot be resolved after the extension, the competition department will schedule a rematch before the competition the following week.

(4) The competition rules will follow the latest soccer rules as reviewed and approved by the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation.

Article 7: Basketball Championship

(1) Each team is limited to 10 registered players for men and 12 for women.

(2) Women's games will use a six-player, two-zone center jump ball system.

(3) The competition will use an elimination system. The order will be drawn by the competition department. The winner of the final will win the championship.

(4) If two teams are tied, the time should be extended to resolve the tie for men's games. For women's games, a solution should be agreed upon before the game. If the two sides cannot agree, then the men's rules for extending the time will be followed. However, if the tie cannot be resolved after the second extension, the competition department will schedule a rematch before the competition the following week.

(5) The competition rules will follow the latest men's and women's basketball rules as reviewed and approved by the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation.

(1) Divided into singles and doubles. Singles players may also play doubles.

(2) Regardless of singles or doubles, men's games will use a best-of-five set format, and women's games will use a best-of-three set format.

(3) The competition will use an elimination system. The order will be drawn by the competition department. The winner of the final will win the championship.

(4) The competition rules will follow the latest tennis rules as reviewed and approved by the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation. (To be continued)

Diary of the British Wimbledon World Tennis Championships (10)

Special Correspondent from London - Yi Zhi Ji

Friday, July 7th

A great championship final that requires five sets to decide the winner is an uncommon exception. Generally, only three or four sets are needed, and there are few highlights. But at least two historically memorable matches are completely the opposite. In 1919, Lee Williams defeated Johnston at Forest Hills, making a comeback in the fifth set after trailing 0-3. Many spectators said it was the best tennis they had ever seen. Today, Crawford of Sydney, Australia, defeated Barnes, the defending champion and current All-American champion, also requiring five sets to decide the winner. Both players displayed the best tennis ever seen, with the two sides evenly matched, each winning two sets and each winning four games. Spectators said that the match should have ended there, so that neither player would lose their glory.

Barnes (Right) Crawford (Left) Photo before the final

The scene on the court was extremely satisfying. The weather was mild, the sun was shining, and there was a light breeze. The central court was packed with people, the atmosphere was excellent, and the sightlines were also satisfactory. The only flaw was that one of Barnes' shots landed at least two inches beyond the baseline but was not called out. The request for silence from the referee became monotonous, often requiring waiting one or two seconds before calling the decision. The spectators' hopes for a British champion were extremely high, as it had been eleven years since Patterson. The applause for Crawford was deafening, and when the victory was decided, some spectators jumped for joy, some shouted wildly, hats flew in the air, women were crying and laughing, and some even fainted. It was said that Mrs. Crawford was also among them.

Both sides demonstrated the highest level of sportsmanship. After several games on both sides, the two players walked very calmly to the referee's chair, took towels to wipe their sweat, without fear or shame.

After the women's doubles, the two players slowly entered the court. Barnes practiced with McDougall on the outer court, as did Crawford. Then they entered the court at the same time. Crawford brought a towel and both held rackets in their hands. Crawford won the coin toss for the right to serve first. Throughout the five sets, if a set ended with an even number of games, then Crawford would retain the right to serve first.

Barnes won the first set 6-4, and then won his service game after leading 5-2. In the second set, he often attacked, but was strongly resisted by Crawford. Crawford gradually gained control of his opponent's cannonball serve, and then often broke it. Sometimes the ball would stop after hitting the net, and sometimes the ball would return, and so on, until the end of the match. Barnes' scoring on his serve gradually decreased. In addition to this great control of the serve, Crawford's confidence also gradually increased, and his position also advanced to within three to five feet of the baseline. This was nothing less than a replay of the French Three Musketeers Lacoste and Cochet breaking through Tilden's cannonball serve. As Crawford gradually stabilized, Barnes began to waver.

Crawford's first reason for victory was his smooth and solid returns. Unless there was no other way, he never failed to return the ball. Barnes was naturally greatly disappointed, unable to put all his strength into his serve. Initially, it was successful, but as Crawford regained his strength, his success declined accordingly. In the twelfth game of the second set, he made many mistakes and finally could not recover. The third set also belonged to Crawford, and the fourth set to Barnes. After the two sides tied at two sets each, the serious situation was seen. Barnes missed a volley, giving away this important game, otherwise the situation would have been greatly changed. After that, Crawford's situation stabilized and went smoothly. (To be continued on July 7th)

Page 14

Free Talk

The Centennial of Charles' Birth

— Yu Dafu

When Charles (Ferdinand von Saar) is mentioned, people may feel strange, because this name is rarely seen in Chinese literary publications or translations. This is inevitable. Not to mention China, even in English-speaking countries like England and America, where foreign literature is translated and introduced the most, it is unlikely that there will be a translation of Charles's works. But in Germany, especially in his native Austria, he was praised by several knowledgeable critics, both before and after his death, as a first-class immortal writer comparable to Gottfried Keller and Theodor Storm.

Charles was born on September 30, 1833, into an aristocratic family in Vienna. Although it was an aristocratic family that rose from officials, most of whom were incorruptible officials, this Austrian official family had no property; therefore, Charles was forced by livelihood and joined the military at a young age to make a living. In 1860, he was tired of military life and was stirred by his inner impulses. Although he knew that writing was an unreliable way to make a living, he resolutely withdrew from the army and began to work as a writer. At that time, the treatment of writers in Austria was probably worse than in China today. If Charles had not been protected by the two noble ladies, Elisabeth Salm, Countess of Salm, and Josephine von Wertheimstien, he would have starved to death long ago. He wrote many poems and poetic dramas, and many short stories with a limited outline, sad and beautiful, and with an unparalleled tone. He did not receive the praise of some critics until he was sixty years old. In order to commend the achievements of national poets, the Austrian government appointed him as a member of the House of Lords. This was certainly a national special honor unparalleled since the great playwright Grillparzer.

On July 23, 1906, at the age of seventy-three, this lonely great poet, who had long suffered from cancer and remained single, committed suicide with a pistol after going out for a walk in the morning. His complete works in twelve volumes, bound in four books, were published by Max Hesse of Leipzig, with a detailed biography by Anton Bettelheim attached.

He himself thought that his poems and dramas were his most satisfying works, but his immortal fame clearly depended on his dozens of short stories. A special article will be written to introduce his works. Here, only a very rough outline of his life is conveyed to express admiration.

"Only Death is a Profit"

— Yu Jun

In a school's teachers' lounge, although there were many people, only a few were talking and laughing. These were all Hunanese. Hunanese have always stubbornly stuck to their hometown accents until death. Their tones were particularly high, and they loved to compete to speak. Others who wanted to join in the conversation seemed to have no way to participate, and often became dazed and silent. Among this dazed and silent group, there was a man around thirty years old, wearing an untidy Western suit. His beard could never be completely shaved, and it covered his thin, black face in a messy way. His lower jaw protruded slightly outward, causing his two rows of teeth to lose their balance. The lower teeth, like swords and halberds, seemed ready to counterattack upwards, while the upper teeth resisted desperately. Someone came over and introduced him: "This is our fellow townsman, Mr. Peng Jiahua," and I knew he was also from Hunan. After shaking hands and exchanging greetings, he lowered his head and mechanically drew on the tablecloth with chalk, still dazed and silent.

One day, I happened to meet him at the train station, and he ran over.

"Where is XX now?"

"In Shanghai."

"Life is still very difficult, isn't it?"

"Yes."

"Why don't you write for a living?"

"It's also difficult. Materials, talent, and sales are not easy things... "

The train whistled. He hurriedly said goodbye and got on the train. "Yes, he is writing for a living," I thought.

From then on, he was not seen in the teachers' lounge for a long time. I asked someone familiar with him, and they said he felt very bored and resigned. At that time, everyone there seemed to feel very bored, but no one resigned.

As time passed, his image gradually faded in my mind and was forgotten. One day, I suddenly saw the news of his arrest in the newspaper, and I was very surprised. The charges were terribly serious. In fact, this kind of charge, like a prevalent germ, floats around in the world every day. Whoever bumps into it is unlucky, but bumping into his head felt somewhat different. Acquaintances were very worried about him, but he escaped the hand of death as if he had escaped the invasion of germs. After that, I lost contact with him.

Until this year, one day, Mengke came back from outside and said to me, "Do you know Peng Huang?"

"I know him."

"He talked to me about you and wants to come and see you!"

"Hmm."

One day in late August, I had not yet gotten out of bed when a guest came to visit. Upon meeting him, it was indeed Mr. Peng Jiahua. His Western suit was a bit neater, but the rest was the same as before, without much change. However, his face was no longer black, but pale. That deathly pallor made people feel sad. We talked about our situations since we last met, and we were talking happily when another friend came. He became dazed and silent again, and finally couldn't sit still and left.

A few days later, Mengke came again and told me that he was sick, very seriously. I thought I should go see him, but for some reason, I've just been lazy lately, letting the days slip by, until I received the news of his death.

Two weeks ago, wasn't he sitting in the chair I'm sitting in now? Wasn't he still talking about past dreams, future dreams? But now he's dead! He wrote all his life, and everyone is familiar with his name, but no one talks about his work, there is no praise, and no criticism. If this is loneliness, then he worked in loneliness, and died in loneliness! I thought of his dream, I thought of the day Mengke took the quick sketch of him, and he said, "It's very similar, very similar," but too scary, too scary"! Friend, what are you afraid of? You probably still don't know that the place you will eventually reach is right in front of you!

Chekhov, in Rothschild's Fiddle, said, "There is at least one benefit to a person's death: they can't eat, drink, pay taxes, or harm others; moreover, a person sleeps in a grave for more than a year, they can sleep for thousands of years, ten thousand years; for thousands of years, ten thousand years, not eating, drinking, paying taxes, or harming others, what a great benefit that is!" However, Rothschild made coffins for people, made coffins for his wife, and at the same time played the violin in the Jewish band he hated. When he was dying, he couldn't help but think: "Life has just passed like this, without any benefit, without any satisfaction, everything has passed by in a blur, and nothing has been retained." Therefore, Chekhov sighed: "In short, human life is a loss, only death is a profit!" This meaning is very good, but it is very piercing; a person only lives in this world once, why is the world arranged in such a way that he has no benefit in his life?" I will use these words as an elegy for the dead!

Not a Defense

— Lou Jiannan

Someone told me that Mr. Mu wrote an article criticizing my translated book. I knew it must be about 20th-century European literature, because during the period of translating that book, I experienced two major events, the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident. My life was extremely chaotic, but on the one hand, for the sake of livelihood, I had to reluctantly continue that work. I remember on the morning of January 29, 1932, I escaped alone from the artillery alley on North Sichuan Road, leaving everything behind, only taking out that original book. Work accomplished in such a life should naturally accept sincere examination. But today, after seeing Mr. Mu's article, I thought that while translating a work of over 100,000 words does not allow for any mistakes, writing a critique of over 1,000 words also seems to require some prudence. For example, Mr. Mu said that my translation of Msxim du Khan is fabricated. Unfortunately, he did not note the non-fabricated original name, and stubbornly insisted that there is no such person as Maxsim Kahn, as if even the original author, Fréchet, were colluding with me to deceive people. I know that Mr. Mu has a deep understanding of French literature, so why didn't he check carefully? Because at least this name was not fabricated by me. I remember that at that time, I consulted many books just to find the original text of the transliteration of proper nouns. Regarding Kahn, it was probably based on the Xiaoshuo Yuebao World Literature issue (20th Anniversary Publication). From this point, I wonder whether Mr. Mu's other original text comparisons are all reliable. Unfortunately, I don't even have the leisure to find my own translation and the original text. Fortunately, there are many new tasks to be done, and it is not necessary to defend my past. Moreover, I knew from the beginning that the translation was a thankless task, so even if Mr. Mu's criticism is a bit reckless, I can sincerely accept it.

Words of a Bibliomaniac

— A Ying

In the past, there were many bibliomaniacs who had a very strong interest in books. In old poems, the so-called "diligently reading thousands of volumes," and "spending all the gold to collect books," are all about how passionate these people were about books. However, this is said of people who had money to buy books. Those who didn't have money to buy books couldn't do that. Some of them ran to bookstores and stood there "skimming" to read, some stood with their hands behind their backs, staring blankly at the book titles on the shelves, some ran hundreds of miles to beg for mercy at the doors of book collectors, and some, as Guo Moruo wrote, found a good opportunity to "shoplift" the books they loved. People without money also had their own ways. These things are scattered in ancient books and are very interesting. From this, we can see how many people who worked hard in their studies used to overcome the difficulties of not having books with such arduous spirit. Although I myself have not achieved anything in my studies, I have been constantly walking this difficult path. Therefore, when reading, I pay special attention to this kind of event. Now, I will write down the more meaningful parts and make it into a "Words of a Bibliomaniac!" Among the readers, there will probably be no shortage of people who like to read such stories. This can be considered a "preface."

II

At the end of the Ming Dynasty, the richest book collection south of the Yangtze River belonged to Qian Muzhai. He had many fine Song and Yuan editions. Unfortunately, he encountered a fire, and these books were turned to ashes, except for those in the eastern city. Among them was a Song edition of the History of the Former and Later Han Dynasties of the Northern Song Dynasty. Muzhai bought this book for only three hundred taels of gold, because two volumes of the "History of the Later Han Dynasty" were missing, and the seller specially reduced the price. Muzhai regarded this book as very precious and entrusted many booksellers to find the missing volumes to complete it. One of them, on one occasion, stopped his boat in Wuzhen and went ashore to buy noodles for dinner. The noodle shop owner took out two books from a broken basket as wrapping paper. The bookseller saw that they were Song editions of the "History of the Later Han Dynasty," and they were precisely the two volumes Muzhai was missing. He was very happy and negotiated with the noodle shop owner, spending "a few coins" to buy them. But one of the volumes was missing the first page. He asked the noodle shop owner, who said that the neighbor across the street had just asked him to wrap the noodles, so the bookseller went to the neighbor across the street and asked for that page as well. He rushed to Changzhou overnight and delivered it to Muzhai. Muzhai was overjoyed and threw a good banquet to treat him to dinner, and gave him twenty taels of gold. This book was taken away by "those in important positions" in the early Qing Dynasty. So it is recorded in the "Anecdotes of Muzhai."

Shallow Lake (II)

— Written by Joseph Conrad, translated by Shi Heng

This narrow tributary is like a ditch: winding and bottomless in its depths; under the narrow, clear, cyan canopy of the sky, it is filled with dimness. Huge trees, hidden behind the dense net of vines, stand tall. Near the glittering black water, amidst the network of small ferns, one can see the distorted roots of large trees everywhere, gloomy and dark, still and winding, like captured snakes. The short words of the boatmen echoed in the thick, dim grass walls. Darkness, from among the trees, through the tangled thickets of vines, from behind the fantastically still, large leaves, flowed out; this darkness, mysterious and invisible, is like the darkness of the fragrant and poisonous forest where one cannot set foot.

The boatmen pushed their poles in the shallow water, and the gap opened up, forming a vast, still lake. The forest retreated from the damp shore, leaving a green meadow of reeds, reflecting the cyan of the sky. A woolly, peach-colored cloud floated in the sky, reflecting the subtle colors of the floating clouds below the leaves of the lotus flowers and the silver blossoms. A small house built on stakes looked dark and hollow from a distance. Next to the house, two tall palm trees, as if reaching up from behind the forest, leaned on the uneven roof. The tilt of the leafy and towering tree tops made it seem as if they had sorrowful thoughts.

The helmsman, pointing with his paddle, said, "Asat's house is over there. I saw his boat tied to the stakes."

The boatmen ran along the edge of the boat, turning their faces to look at the end of their day's journey. They would rather spend the night anywhere than in this eerie and legendary haunted shallow lake. In addition, they didn't like Asat, first because he was a stranger, and second because he repaired a damaged house and lived in it, and claimed that he was not afraid to live with the spirits that bewitched this abandoned place. Such a person would disrupt the direction of fate with his eyes and words; at the same time, the spirits he was familiar with were not easy to reconcile with passing travelers, and they often wanted to avenge their masters on passers-by. White people do not believe these things, because they are pagans, and are allied with the "spirit master", so the "spirit master" will make them safely cross this fantastic land. If righteous people warn them, they pretend not to believe it. What else can be done?

The boatmen pondered in this way as they pushed their poles. The large dugout canoe quickly, quietly, and smoothly moved towards Asat's reclaimed land, until the dropped pole made a loud sound, and people murmured, "Allah, praise be!" The boat gently bumped against the stakes, reaching the bottom of the house.

The boatmen looked up and shouted discordantly, "Asat! Hey, Asat!" But no one came. The white man began to climb the ladder on the bamboo platform in front of the house. The captain said unhappily, "We will cook on the sampan and sleep on the water." "Pass me the blankets and baskets," the white man said listlessly.

He knelt on the edge of the bamboo platform and took the things. Then the boat moved, and the white man stood up, facing Asat, because he had already walked out of the small doorway of the house. He was a strong and vigorous young man, with a broad chest and muscular arms. He was wearing only a pair of shorts. His head was shaved. His large, gentle eyes were intensely fixed on the white man, but his voice and attitude did not contain a trace of courtesy; he suddenly asked:

"Do you have medicine with you, Tu An?"

"No," the visitor said in a surprised tone. "No. What's wrong? Is there a patient in this house?" "Go in and see," Asat said in the same calm tone, then suddenly turned and walked into the door of the house. The white man, putting down his luggage, followed him.

Financial Foreign Cables Unfavorable, Panic, Spot Gold Falls by Ten Dollars and Four Cents

Pittman Suggests Raising the Price of Silver

US Secretary of Agriculture Indicates Inflationary Currency

Yesterday, the gold market weakened due to the contraction of the overseas silver market in England and the United States. Exchange rates also fell. The forward silver price on the Five Metals Exchange fell by 1.7 to 2.5 cents. The private cable silver price contracted by 1875. US cotton fell by 14-15 points per pound. US wheat contracted by 1/125. Stocks rose and fell. London bullion was also cheap. The opening offer was stable, but it was only a flash in the pan and immediately fell below 30 yuan. This was because reports indicated that US Senator Pittman had submitted a plan to President Roosevelt. If adopted, the price of silver could be raised to $1.19 per ounce. Many small investors frantically shorted. However, large players maintained the price by buying on dips. The opening was still flat. After the opening, it remained flat. By the time HSBC quoted the exchange rate, it had not moved. After the announcement, the exchange market suddenly hardened. Reuters reported that US Secretary of Agriculture Wallace indicated that there may be currency inflation within three months. The main method was to minimize the gold content in US dollars. Rumors spread, triggering a slump. However, there were still several rebounds. The market was flat and then epidemic, with extreme panic. Small investors desperately pressed down, but they were always at a disadvantage. After the close, it was even worse. The premium price was increased by 270 yuan. Contents of Silver Coin Assays for August

According to the Central Mint Assay Committee's August review of legal new coins, totaling 3,840,000 yuan, as reported in the previous issue, a sample of 397 silver dollars was taken for assay. The average fineness was found to be 880.56, exceeding the standard by 0.063%. The average pure silver content per coin was 22.507166 grams, exceeding the standard weight by 0.013718, or 0.058%. The average weight was 26.6957 grams, falling short of the standard by 0.0014, or 0.005%.

Bond Market Shrouded in Securities Rumors

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw relatively active trading, but market prices remained weak. Rumors circulated that the government would issue new public bonds. However, after inquiries by reporters, it was said that the Central Political Council had decided not to issue new public bonds temporarily to avoid increasing the burden on the public. Despite this, market prices continued to decline. The fundamental situation had not changed, but there were speculations that the government might continue to issue 50 million yuan of 20-year disaster relief bonds to make up for the previous incomplete issuance. Whether this speculation is accurate remains to be seen. Yesterday's market performance showed that during the morning session, scattered buyers were not inactive in the initial trading. Prices for consolidation bonds to the 1929 Customs Bonds rose by ten cents to forty cents. As trading shifted to the twenty-year bonds, sellers gradually emerged, and market prices declined. Market sentiment shifted, with more empty positions. Prices gradually fell, retracing by ten cents to thirty-five cents. During the afternoon session, all factions shifted their strategies, leaning towards selling. Major players began selling off, and prices continued to fall by ten cents to forty-five cents. The afternoon session saw sales of issues 31 and 38, with lingering unease and few buyers. The trend remained uncertain, and prices continued to fall slightly by twenty or thirty cents. At the close, only the Salt Tax bonds showed a slight rebound of five to ten cents, while other issues remained weak, generally falling by ten to twenty cents. Short-selling of gold was most prevalent, with a total decrease of over seventy cents for the day, while other issues fell by fifteen cents to sixty cents. The market did not experience a major crash. The total transaction volume was 9,221,000 yuan, including 6,000 yuan in spot transactions. Futures trading included 3,490,000 yuan for Salt Tax, 1,330,000 yuan for Military Reorganization bonds, 1,245,000 yuan for the 1929 Customs Bonds, 1,735,000 yuan for the 20-year and 20-year Customs Bonds, and varying amounts from tens of thousands to three or five hundred thousand yuan for other issues. The exchange's stock was traded at 59 yuan for ten shares.

Cocoon merchants are selectively weighing and purchasing only the best cocoons. Edible Oil: Tung Oil Gradually Declines

| Foreign Firms Remain Inactive; Domestic Merchants Seize the Opportunity to Buy In |

After the foreign transaction price of white tung oil in Hankou reached 27.23 yuan per dan, the market became silent. Hankou merchants, seeing this situation, knew that a continued decline in prices was necessary to stimulate buyers' interest, so they immediately lowered the price to 26 yuan, but there were still no transactions. Now the price has fallen to 25 yuan. It is uncertain whether this will stimulate transactions, but even if there are still no transactions, or only a few, the market can stabilize and not decline further. Moreover, such a sharp decline may be an attempt by merchants to buy in order to build up a large inventory and prepare for demand from foreign firms. Otherwise, the decline would not be so large.

Customers' goods have also gradually declined as a result. Southern branch tung oil has fallen from 21.78 yuan and 21.34 yuan to 21 yuan, and then to 20.78 yuan in recent days. Xiangtung tung oil has also gradually declined from 21.78 yuan to 19.67 yuan today. All are customer prices. Only a week has passed, but the prices have fallen so sharply, which was really unexpected. It is said that merchants have opened up about 6,000 to 7,000 dan in this falling price environment, and the inventory has been prepared, only waiting for buyers. Therefore, it is quite accurate to say that this decline is manipulated by Hankou merchants. Local merchants in Shanghai, because it is already autumn, do not have abundant inventory, so there may be some who take this opportunity to buy, but they are generally unwilling to stock up too much. As for Zhejiang tung oil, although there are not many goods, it cannot but follow suit with the decline in Hankou. Therefore, according to reports from Hangzhou merchants, the price has also loosened to about 23 yuan per piece. It is only because sales in various places are sporadic, and there are no large numbers of transactions.

Essays

Man is Inferior to a Dog

-- Shen Yan

"Man is inferior to a dog" is not an idiom, nor has it ever been found in the great works of scholars of the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties. Of course, it is not a historical allusion. However, we can often see or hear it. When mentioned, it seems very familiar. The reason is not very complex, only because people often use this sentence as an expression of deep emotion.

The emotion expressed by this sentence can be further divided into two types: one is mostly from expressions of admiration for dogs. These are mostly uttered by poor people living in harsh conditions and facing economic difficulties. For example, coolies and laborers, although they have five senses and four limbs, fully resembling humans, their enjoyment is truly worlds apart compared to the dogs kept by wealthy families. Similarly, we brain-working laborers often rely on our legs to walk when we go out. If we are unlucky enough to walk on a street with a lot of sewage, we are carefully moving forward along the edge of the street with our heads lowered, but a 1932 or 1933 automobile suddenly flies over from behind. The four wheels splash the mud on the street to both sides like electric fans. When you are splashed with countless specks of mud and look back with an angry gaze, you will often see a large or small dog with a slightly different appearance sitting leisurely in the car, coldly smiling at you. At this time, the emotion comes: "Man is inferior to a dog!"

The other type is an expression of cursing people. For example, you sacrifice one or two bowls of white rice every day to raise a dog, and it can always help you a little at night. Even if it doesn't help you, it will never turn around and bite you! Unfortunately, you make a black-hearted friend. Although you treat him with the utmost kindness, he uses vicious means to seize your property or injure your life! At that time, the people around you and yourself will inevitably say, "Man is inferior to a dog" to express their emotions.

In the past, I often used the phrase "Man is inferior to a dog" to express envy for dogs, but I never used it to curse people because I felt that although there really are people who are inferior to dogs, they are, after all, a small minority. In order to maintain the dignity of us humans, it is best to avoid expressing this emotion. However, in recent years, the human news that I have seen in newspapers has been almost entirely of behaviors that "even beasts would disdain to do." Seducing a sister-in-law and killing a brother, an adulterous woman killing her husband, cases involving corpses in boxes... they emerge endlessly. Not to mention that dogs would never do such things, even wolves and tigers might not be so cruel. Therefore, recently I have had a new awakening. I think that no matter how much wealthy people's dogs sit in cars, eat gourmet food, or even wear Western clothes, we are not qualified to envy them. We should examine ourselves. Do modern people's character measure up to dogs?

Storm

-- Fu Yizhi

The sequence of seasons is advancing like rubber wheels. The fiery summer has quietly disappeared without us realizing it, and the line of poetry "the sound of insects newly penetrates the green window screen" has been seized by writers to embellish articles of the "early autumn occasional feelings" type to stir up a commotion. Alas! "Yesterday's youth is today's white hair" cannot help but make me shudder at the brevity of life and the arduousness of responsibility.

However, although the season has reached early autumn, the climate is not changing rapidly. I mechanically continue to do very minor desk work, and the stinky sweat evaporated by the water in my body is still constantly flowing out from my thirty-six thousand pores.

It was an afternoon, and the stuffy air was suffocating. I knew that this was an inevitable process of climate change when it wants to cool down but is still hot, and it was a sign of a storm. We don't need to be annoyed, and we don't need to curse. We just need to endure temporarily. This climate, which is about to decline, will soon be swept away by the storm. I predicted this.

I walked out of the dark room. Ragged clouds covered the entire sky. The terrifying sunlight occasionally shone down a line of intense light from the gaps in the clouds, but it was soon densely blocked by the thick clouds and could no longer exert its authority.

Thunder rumbled like a war drum, and lightning flickered and twisted incessantly in the gray and black clouds. Undoubtedly, it was the harbinger of the storm. A pitch-black cloud in the southeast corner hung down a few sparse lines of rain, extending straight to this land where heat was lurking. Then, a few gusts of strong wind blew, and bean-sized raindrops, along with the dense black clouds, spread out their formation and shot down relentlessly. Pedestrians scurried around like birds and beasts in the face of a great disaster.

The earth became even darker. The garbage on the road was washed to both sides by the rainwater. The accumulated water in the puddles, under the attack of raindrops, overflowed with bubbles of colored light. Brave rickshaw pullers, pulling their rickshaws, braved the wind and rain and struggled to compete in a long-distance race with the speeding Austins. Lovers of a leisurely life hid in shops and alleys, impatiently watching, regretting, and cursing!

Friends! Light is behind the darkness; the storm is the "salvation army" that changes the climate. We cannot wait long, so let's move forward with the storm!

"Generous Charity" and "Robots"

— Zhu Yan

A certain Mr. said: "Nowadays, modern students are truly generous, continuously sending large sums of money earned by their parents through sweat and blood, term after term, into the school's accounting office coffers, without any stinginess. This allows the principal to sit in a small Austin car, the professors' wives to have enough money to buy high-heeled leather shoes, and the snot-nosed sons of the school workers and tea servers not to cry about being hungry. The students themselves sit high and mighty in the classroom, swinging their legs, chatting and laughing, writing 'Sweetheart,' humming 'Dream Lover.' The professors, feeling grateful, want to reciprocate with some 'knowledge' as a gift, but the students are polite, returning it all. Therefore, on their graduation diplomas, after four years, the words 'Generous Charity' should be added to commend their benevolent spirit."

A certain student said: "Who says that Europeans and Americans create, Japanese imitate, and Chinese don't create?" Now, the Chinese ability to imitate is thousands and millions of times greater than that of the short Japanese. Look! Europeans and Americans invented "robots" not long ago, and the Japanese haven't even succeeded in imitating them yet, but we Chinese have already produced and applied them in large quantities. If you don't believe me, look at those on the podiums in schools across the country, gesticulating, shaking their heads, reciting textbooks verbatim, directly reading from lecture notes. Aren't they all completely and utterly authentic "flesh robots?"

Eating Peace

— Zui Zhu

Every year in the seventh month, we celebrate the Taiping Gong Festival, the Ullambana Festival. Even just releasing a single Flaming Mouth is a fixed income for the "local associates," "beggar leaders," and "rascals." In general, it's called "eating peace."

Every year, according to old customs, in the seventh month of the lunar calendar, everyone chips in sixty or seventy cash coins to buy a few sheets of "yellow paper" and binds them into a crooked donation book. They write a few large, "ghostly" characters - Ullambana Festival - and bring the old donation book along. ... In this way, they can set out to solicit money and carry out their "calling for peace" work.

When this "peace troupe" sets out, they also cooperate and divide the work, each with their own responsibilities: one carries a long bamboo pole, ready to hang paper ingots; one swings a large bag, ready to store money and tin foil; and one holds the donation book, going door-to-door to solicit donations – that's the leader of the peace troupe.

"Ah! Excuse me, we have to bother you again. According to old customs, at the entrance of this alley, we need to release a 'Flaming Mouth' to provide relief to the lonely souls and protect the peace of the population..." These few words are their "door-knocking speech," used at every household. After saying this, without waiting for the homeowner to speak, they open the old book and say, "Last year, you gave four dimes. This year, everything is more expensive, so let's raise it a little and write eight dimes, right? This is a good deed, this is..."

If the homeowner doesn't agree, the one swinging the bag will try to persuade them, still writing down four dimes as before. If they agree, then next year it must be eight dimes, this is the "old custom." So their donation amount only increases and never decreases.

They write it down at each house, either money or ingots, until they have written at all the houses they want to write at; fortunately, they are "geographical ghosts," knowing who has just moved in, who is an old resident, who has money, who is embarrassed. They know everything completely, even more clearly than the nominal "household register." So when soliciting, they adapt to the situation, giving according to the person, and have some qualifications, and will never cause trouble.

On the appointed day, they get a few monks and release a Flaming Mouth. Then, on the bridgehead or alley entrance, they post a reimbursement statement, which is the ultimate "public service."

Don't underestimate this "reimbursement statement"; its function is the same as a "stock report" certified by an accountant in a bank. Both can consolidate credit and attract cash.

The Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: The Guest Leaves with a Shy Smile and Tender Feelings; A Visitor Brings Old News, a Sinister Letter Opens Sadness

Zhao Ziqiang threw the end of the cigarette he was holding in his hand on the ground, stamped it out with his foot, and then coughed slightly twice before smiling and saying: I originally had a lot of things to say, but I'm very clumsy with words, and I simply don't know where to start. Guizhi still bit her lip, smiling slightly, and didn't answer the question. Zhao Ziqiang said seriously: I was originally tired of this military life and planned to quit. But a military officer's body isn't as free as a civil official's. Moreover, the company commander is the officer closest to the soldiers, and the company commander, the sergeant, the quartermaster, and the platoon leader all have some connection. Changing a company commander means a lot of trouble, and it's not easy to resign. Without a special reason, the superior won't approve it. There's only one way: first, take a short leave, leave the army, and then slowly write letters to the camp asking for sick leave. No matter how much the army can't let you go, they can't ask a sick person to be a company commander, right? Only then did Guizhi squeeze out a sentence, smiling slightly: A healthy person, why are you talking about getting sick? After he finished speaking, he still lowered his head. Zhao Ziqiang said: That's what I say and what I do, but my father probably won't be happy about it. But apart from this method, wanting to resign is really not easy. Guizhi said: That's okay. He quickly snatched up these four words, but there was no follow-up. What does "that's okay" mean? Does it mean that it's okay if the old man isn't happy? Or does it mean that apart from this method, you can't resign? If that's the case, then you have to force a resignation! Therefore, Zhao Ziqiang just stared at Guizhi in a daze, unable to say anything more. Guizhi seemed to see his meaning, looked at him and smiled, and wanted to say something, but held it back. Zhao Ziqiang said: Didn't I say that I'm a clumsy person, I can't say what I want to say, please forgive me if anything happens. (184)

Little Knowledge

Medicinal Effects of Seasonal Vegetables

— Chu Yu

Nowadays, ordinary meals during the transition between summer and autumn, whether for the propertied or the propertyless class, generally include eggplants, pumpkins, winter melons, watermelons, cucumbers and other vegetables. However, we Chinese people, for any kind of food, only seek the goodness of taste and do not understand the function of various foods, so we see these vegetables as worthless. In fact, for many ailments we have, without spending a penny, we can get very effective medicine, especially in poor rural areas, when suffering from chronic diseases and unable to afford a doctor, we can make use of waste. Now I have a few secret prescriptions that I have invented to introduce to society, please test them one by one, and you will know that my words are true.

(Pumpkin) Chop very ripe pumpkin meat into pieces, dry it in the sun, grind it into a fine powder, which can cure tapeworm disease. Dosage: Take two or three qian with plain boiled water every day, and the tapeworm will come down from the stool. If you dry the pumpkin seeds in the sun (do not wash them with water), simmer them with rock sugar in soup, and take two or three qian every day, you can cure sore throats in children. Also, calcine the pumpkin's crown into ash and swallow two or three qian with plain boiled water every day, which has the effect of resolving phlegm, even greater than the Banxia sold in the market.

(Cucumber) Collect very ripe cucumbers whose exterior has turned yellow-brown, peel off the skin, dig out the seeds, chop the meat into pieces, put them in a magnetic earthenware jar, seal it with paper to prevent air from escaping, and put it in a cool place. If you encounter burns or scalds, take out the rotten, smelly juice and apply it to the injured area, which can not only relieve pain, but also smooth and remove the scars of the wound. Also, collect the tender leaves of cucumbers and dry them in the hot sun, and decoct five or six qian with boiled water every day, which can cure urinary problems and beriberi.

(Watermelon) Generally, for people with leukorrhea, eating more watermelon is very effective. Also, squeeze out the watermelon juice and boil it to make watermelon rind candy, which can be used to treat kidney disease. If you dry the watermelon rind in the sun, decoct five qian with boiled water every day, you can cure edema-related diseases. Also, calcine the watermelon rind into ash, mix it with honey, and if a child suffers from oral sores, applying it is very effective.

(Loofah) Squeeze the juice of ripe and tender loofah, filter it with cloth to clarify it, or take the juice from its stems, which can be used as a cosmetic water. If children get prickly heat in summer, wiping it with this melon juice will immediately relieve it.

(Winter melon) Among vegetables, winter melon has the greatest medicinal effect. If you suffer from nephritis, pleurisy, peritonitis, beriberi and other diseases, it is very effective. If you accidentally eat fish or crab and get poisoned, decoct winter melon juice and take it to detoxify. Winter melon seeds can also cure appendicitis. The so-called 'intestinal decoction' in the past was made with winter melon seeds, moutan bark, peach kernel, and coix seed. (Corn) People with kidney disease, decoct corn with water every day to use as tea, which is both delicious and can treat the disease. If you decoct the corn silk (i.e. pistil) with water, it is also miraculously effective. If you decoct the roots and stems of corn, you can treat bladder stones.

(Eggplant) Eggplant is originally a poisonous plant. Usually, because it is boiled and harmonized with salt and vinegar, the toxic components are broken down. If you burn the eggplant into ash and calcine it, for people suffering from swollen and painful gums, rubbing it with ash is very effective. Also, squeeze out the eggplant juice and apply it to warts once or twice a day, which can also cure them. Also, dry the eggplant flowers in the shade, decoct them with boiling water, which can cure appendicitis and abdominal pain caused by parasites, etc. Decoction of eggplant stems and leaves, applied to frostbite, is more effective than any frostbite medicine.

Talking Points

Talking About "Hope"

— Zhi

It seems I once heard someone say that "hope" is the "lighthouse" of life. A person without "hope" is like a poor person groping in the dark: he has no light, no breath, and no strength! Because with "hope," there is a direction and action to pursue, and finally, the great, eternally indestructible "force" that creates everything is generated!

However, it also seems that some people say that China is the most hopeful and the most capable of "hoping" nation. Indeed, since "September 18th" when Japanese soldiers seized "Shenyang" in the time it took "Young Marshal Zhang" to watch a play, the Chinese people began to live in fervent and sincere "hope": hoping that the "League of Nations" would uphold justice, forcing Japan to return "the three northeastern provinces," so that they themselves would not have to fire a bullet or injure a soldier; hoping that "Soviet Russia" would send troops to "Manchuria" to poke the Japanese in the rear, so that the "Volunteer Army" could win victories in the "green gauze tents"; hoping that a "national hero" would be generous and enthusiastic, regarding death as homecoming, and lead 120,000 soldiers out of the customs to recover the lost land; hoping that the brave and divine "Broadsword Teams" could all "roll eighteen times on the spot" and roll into the enemy's line to chop off the enemy's heads and legs! They even hoped that heaven would open its eyes and the bodhisattvas would show their holiness, causing a major earthquake and a widespread plague in Japan! They also hoped that the "swordsmen" and "real people" in the fairy and martial arts novels who could "fly over walls and walk over roofs" and "spit swords and refine qi" would lead heavenly soldiers and generals to appear in the world and, with a "finger of the right hand," "kill" with "a ray of white light," followed by the heads of the dwarf soldiers and dwarf generals rolling all over the fields, the corpses filling the valleys, and the fresh blood flowing like ditches and like the Yellow River!

"January 28th" arrived. The XX Route Army won a victory, so the "hope" of the Chinese people became even greater! In addition to the previous pile of "hope" that of course had to be retained, many new "hopes" were produced: hoping that the XX Route Army would strike Yangshupu in one breath, hoping that the Japanese soldiers would retreat onto warships and escape outside Wusongkou, hoping to see "five enemy planes shot down" or "ten" in the newspaper every morning, even though we had no anti-aircraft guns;

hoping that the Hunan people would be willing to lend the road to Zhang XX, who was "begging to fight against Japan," to send troops to Shanghai to help, and also hoping that "Baichuan" and "Liuhe" would "die in battle," hoping that the firecrackers set off in the city that night were really because "our army" had "reached the Bund"! And hoping for reinforcements, hoping that the XX Route Army would come from Kunshan and Nanxiang like riding on clouds and fog, and unknowingly let our second-to-last team open the gate early in the morning to see the XX Route Army, all wearing straw sandals and bamboo hats! Even more hoping that Feng XX's 100,000 troops would descend from the sky when "Liuhe was attacked." Of course, there was also hope that the United States would lend a large number of cannons and bullets to me, that the Germans would come to fire the cannons for me, and that Guangdong would send dozens of planes to fight fiercely with the enemy in the sky. The war stopped, the contract was signed, hoping not to lose power or humiliate the country, hoping that the Japanese would compensate for all losses, and then hoping that everyone would sacrifice their family property, destroy their homes to help the country, and donate money to buy planes...

This chaotic, uncountably vast collection of "hope," of course, is also all "light," "breath," and "strength," only it is "unnecessary" to realize it. Because even though it is unnecessary [to realize it], our purpose is still achieved in the same way, this is the principle of having "heavenly assistance," "divine assistance," and "ghost assistance" in the dark, and this "heaven," "god," and "ghost" are bound to be forever with us "Chinese people"! So some people say: "The puppet state is not a problem. In fifty years, Japan will have to bow its head and obey China. What power can that kid Puyi have?" ...

It's true, "hope" is the "lighthouse" of life! With "hope," there is "light," there is "breath," and there is "strength"! But ah, poor people, if "hope" only turns into "expectation," then will it also emit dazzling "light," unstoppable "breath," and the great power that creates everything? For example, a slave "hopes" that his enslaver will have great compassion to save his life, but gives up the struggle himself. Is this "hope" likely to succeed? Isn't it turning into an eternal, unattainable empty wait? Therefore, if you want to be free, you can only engage with your own "power"! Because only in this way can you gain all sympathy. Expecting-style "hope" that others will help is foolish, self-deceiving, and worthless! Because even if people are willing to help, those who exert themselves to help have another purpose, at least, that is, to repeat and replace the position of a previous enslaver!

Opening Ceremony

— Li Li

"Dang! Dang! Dang!" The bell kept ringing, once twice...three in a group, five in a pile, quietly in the playground, the students in the classroom were swallowed into the door of the auditorium like fish, white shirts, black skirts, floral qipaos disappeared at the door, the lingering sound of the bell, buzzing, lingering, scattered in the silent air.

Black heads, high and short, unevenly moving:

Shiny wooden combs, floral ribbons, wavy curled beautiful hair, straight and loose long hair, short, downy, childlike hair...the wave of hair, moving with the movement of the head, constantly moving.

Singing the party song, saluting, reciting the Premier's will, silence. Standing, each black head lowered, long hair draped over the face, itchy, raising a hand to sweep back, the elbow touching the head next door, a hiss sound, embarrassed, apologizing with a low laugh. Again, quiet. Feet lightly drawing, one stroke to the left, one stroke to the right.

"Deng" - the leather shoes kissed the stool leg, black and shiny eyes shot over, rose-colored blush printed on the lowered cheeks. ...

The principal's report: "Students..." The gentle, slight, native-accented Mandarin came out of his mouth... Raising their heads, naively staring at the principal's mouth, listening intently (?) Lowering their heads, looking at their own feet, the students' feet, the teachers' feet, the principal's feet, as if trying to get something from these many different feet. The report is over, the suffocating silent air loosens a little, the wave of heads, the wave of hair move slightly once or twice. Reported! The shiny bald head swaying on the black long gown, the heavy, slow, old voice, incessantly talking, seemingly tireless, seemingly without end. Looking at the watch, five minutes, ten minutes, half past, still the same heavy, slow, old voice, incessantly talking. The floral handkerchief constantly swaying in the hand, sometimes letting go, sometimes folding well; wrapped around the fingers, one wrap to the left, one wrap to the right. Two heads leaning together, talking quietly, extremely faint, traveling-like laughter, coming out of the seam of the leaning heads. ...

The incessant sound, like a string broken - waking up as if from a dream, looking around blankly. Dismissal, a sound like an alarm bell aroused people's spirits. Too tired! Sitting for three whole hours.

White shirts, black skirts, floral qipaos, stirred again by the autumn wind, fluttering in the playground.

Is it Really True that "Suffering" is Predestined?

— Xiao Zhi

Early in the morning, Old Uncle Li, sitting upright at the back door with his copper-rimmed glasses, holding the old Shenbao and reading it word by word in a vague voice, met me coming out to relieve myself. He kept swaying his three-inch long, snow-white beard and shaking his head, extremely emotionally and as if he had seen through this wonderful world, stubbornly grabbing me and saying:

"The Chinese people must have committed some major sins in their previous lives, that's why the King of Hell sent us to the human world to suffer this layer of endless suffering, to endure this lifelong, inexhaustible torment; alas! The Chinese people's suffering is predestined from the previous life!"

I have never believed in "fate" and I most dislike hearing about "fate," and this old uncle was also vaguely talking about "previous lives," "sins," "King of Hell," and "human world." This made my head swell and I felt even more. I really hated him, but I had no choice but to perfunctorily answer him:

"Um... Uncle Li..."

At the same time, I unconsciously shifted my gaze to the newspaper held in his dry and trembling hand. I seemed to have discovered something, I couldn't help but question his "fate" judgment and cried out in shock:

"Ah! Look! Today's newspaper again has a big headline saying, 'The Yellow River in Western Shandong has overflowed, and two million people are about to drown' news!"

"That's right! The Chinese people committed sins in their previous lives, and not small ones! This is clear evidence that the King of Hell is calling us to suffer and endure hardships! Otherwise, why would the Water Dragon Essence be born two years ago, causing national floods, and the deaths of so many people were not enough? Last year, the Old Heavens sent the Star of Slaughter, the Japanese, down to earth to massacre the lives of those in Shanghai, followed by the autumn harvest harming the farmers, and not long ago Wuhan was plagued by floods, and now the Yellow River has breached its banks again, and as many as two million people are suffering? Other phenomena such as the unequal distribution of suffering and happiness in society, and those killed on the battlefield in recent decades, have become even more violent in the past two years, with innocent civilians in the war zone being dragged away to be bandits and killed! This is definitely not an ordinary thing, it must be that fate is predestined, and there is no way to escape."

He spoke so anxiously that he choked a little; his large, drooping black eyeballs stared under his wrinkled eyelids, and finally, he closed his eyes and sighed. I was silent for a while, and I retorted him in a humorous tone:

"Then, Uncle Li, the day before yesterday the newspaper said that the cannon on the warship fired, and the cannonball shot out from behind the cannon's ass, killing several soldiers. Does this mean that these wronged ghosts also had a predestined fate of suffering?"

"..." Uncle Li only nodded, his expression very solemn. But, I couldn't bear it any longer, and I also had the intention of awakening this numb, pitiful old man who was already halfway into the coffin. However, my words were extremely gentle and smooth, and extremely serious:

"Uncle Li, do you really believe that fate is predestined from a previous life? It's all the same principle, 'fate' is just the anesthetic used by ambitious people to deceive us weaklings! They use this life-taking anesthetic to allow us to calmly and obediently accept oppression and be slaughtered,

and they can also be at ease and happily and constantly use poisonous sticks to whip us, they know that we are believers in "fate theory," knowing that we, in addition to docile groaning and wailing, are at most too afraid to even struggle. But Uncle Li, people are always people, we should resolutely blot out the two words "fate" with thick ink, roll up our sleeves and use our own inherent strength to drive all obstacles behind us, and step on them hard with our heels..."

My words were not finished, his uncle seemed very tired, he yawned several times in a row, he interrupted my words, stubbornly saying:

"Idle talk idle talk! I've talked for several decades more than you, probably thinking more clearly than you, do you know that nothing in the world is not precisely determined by fate? "Fate" is the truest thing!"

"Then, Uncle Li, is the 'suffering fate' of the Chinese people really predestined..." I said...

Ancient Temple

— Bing

North of Shanghai, there is an ancient temple with crumbling walls and faint traces of bullets.

It is difficult to call it ancient, yet it does not display any divine power. Therefore, the nearby residents do not quite believe in it. When something happens, they prefer to go far away to other temples to pray. The incense smoke here has always been very sparse. During the Shanghai Battle, among the many temples, only this one was destroyed by artillery fire, which shows that the bodhisattvas inside the temple have no mighty power. It has been a year and a half since it was destroyed, and no one, neither devout women nor pious men, has come forward to advocate for its reconstruction. As a result, it remains a ruin with crumbling walls and faint traces of bullets.

"Although the temple is ancient, it does not display any divine power" has become a common saying among the residents of the surrounding area.

According to legend, this ancient temple has a restriction: young women are not allowed to enter. Therefore, when sincere women want to offer incense, ask about their fortune, or pray for children, they must ask middle-aged women who are past their prime to enter the temple and pray on their behalf. They themselves can only stand at the temple entrance, devoutly gazing at the statues of the gods inside, silently praying.

Why this is the case, the nearby residents are somewhat uncertain.

Only one night before the Shanghai Battle, the old monk Deshan in the temple, while performing a Qingjiao ritual for the noodle shop across the street owned by A Qiu, mentioned a little about it to the boss: "During the Revolution of 1911, a young woman went wild in the temple." As to how she went wild, the old monk did not elaborate. When A Qiu pressed him, the old monk cut him off, saying, "The ancient temple is no longer very divine. We are sincerely protecting the Way. Don't mention such things again."

This restriction has been passed down for more than twenty years, and indeed, no one dared to violate it lightly.

However, since the Shanghai Battle, the ancient temple has become a war ruin, and the old monk who maintained the restriction has disappeared without a trace. His life or death is unknown, and the restriction has become an unclosed opening. As a result, young women often enter to take a look, as if exploring a secret.

Soon after, a new monk arrived, claiming to have come from a famous mountain. However, he did not understand poetry or books, and he could barely speak his own name clearly. During the day, he went out, saying he was soliciting donations to rebuild the temple, but A Qiu said he had seen him begging in the concession.

The new monk was very amiable. During such scorching summer days, he did not refuse the many residents who came to the temple to sleep in the open at night. He only said, at first, that he found it somewhat inappropriate that many boys and girls were running around naked. However, he merely gave two such warnings: "This will not be allowed in the future, once the temple is rebuilt!"

One night, after a violent storm, the number of people sleeping in the open decreased. Only a couple of coolies were lying on the front steps of the main hall, and their two children beside them were also dressed in clothes and trousers, as well-behaved as two lazy cats asleep. Elsewhere, in a clean open space above, a middle-aged poor woman was also sleeping, her breasts exposed. Her husband had originally been sleeping with her, but he had rushed back to his own thatched hut before the storm to fix the leaks, and he had not returned since.

After the storm, heat rose from the ground, and the stars in the sky twinkled. The new monk, sleeping in the half-collapsed outhouse, felt an infinite sense of oppression and trouble. His Buddhist heart kept pounding. Although he kept fanning his palm with a black folding fan and chanting Amitabha, his heart could not calm down. Under the light waves of the stars, he vaguely glimpsed the breasts of the middle-aged poor woman. Suddenly, her snoring drew out a long breath, and his Buddhist heart flashed. He closed his eyes again and chanted Amitabha.

As a result, at daybreak, when the sky was already fish-belly white, many people surrounded the new monk in the clean open space above, scolding him and hitting him. He only chanted Amitabha.

"Even monks do this. No wonder the ancient temple has become like this today!" It was an old woman standing to the side, who had seen through the essence of Zen, muttering to herself.

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy

— Mr. Li Zhongjie's Painting

(Brief Biography)

Li, with the style name Zhongjie, was born handsome and with extraordinary strength. He loved ancient paintings and calligraphy and formed the Songfeng Painting and Calligraphy Society as an elegant gathering with friends. His family was wealthy, and he gradually collected works. He then extensively imitated the valuable traces of the ancients and gained considerable insight. His strength lay in boldness, so large-scale works were his forte.

Lucky Child

— Yin

After the school bell rang at four o'clock, I felt extremely lighthearted. Half of my burden was lifted. Although I still had to prepare for night school homework, my exhausted energy should have some comfortable and effective adjustment at this time. So I went alone to the grass field, took a basketball in my hand, and ran alone on the several-zhang-long grass field, playing with the ball. "Ah! How tiring! Playing basketball alone." Those watching me shouted like this, but I only felt it was interesting. I forgot all the troublesome and tiring things. Sweat was flowing, and I was panting, but I didn't feel anything. In my mind, I kept thinking: "Exercise is beneficial to health and indirectly beneficial to studies." After playing basketball for twenty minutes, I changed my approach. I stepped on the seesaw, stepping it successfully to a horizontal line. I stood in the middle point, swaying back and forth, feeling both danger and interest. Later, I went to play on the slide. Everything felt full of interest.

Ah! The joy of studying is endless! Mom said, "Studying can make you a knowledgeable person, and you can occupy an important position in society in the future, truly becoming a useful person for the country. But hope is endless, as long as you grasp reality and work hard in the present, the aspirations of the future are not difficult to achieve, and the happiness of the future can undoubtedly be obtained." I listened to Mom's words, and I couldn't help thinking: How lucky I am, in such a country where education is not widespread, to be able to receive secondary education! How fortunate this is! Yes, I am a lucky child, but there are still a large number of people outside the school gate. How should I treat them? There are many girls who are not powerless to study, but are actually victims trapped in the environment of old ethics. What about "Girls only need to know a few characters! It's enough to read ordinary letters and write daily accounts. Who wants girls to earn a living?" There is also "Going back and forth on the street every day is strangely eye-catching." We think that in these few words, we easily bury the happiness of our girls, letting them grope along the long, dark road. There are also poor children who are powerless to study. They look enviously at the lucky children carrying their schoolbags and going to school, but they themselves are relegated to the ranks of the rejected. They can only watch and drool, and eventually they become "illiterate" and "ignorant." There are too many who suffer like this. But what methods can I think of to save them? Who should be blamed for the lack of widespread education? But the fact is really confusing and contradictory. There are schools everywhere in some places, but the content is unimaginable, just like my previous article "Schools Stand Like Forests," it's terrible! What remedy do these schools that stand like forests provide for reality?···

Drama

War and Peace (Act Two, Three, and Four) — Ling Xia

Act Two: The Fleeing Crowd

Wounded Man: You ask if there are any young women in my family? Let me tell you. I only had a good son, but he died several years ago. He left behind a child, only six years old this year. That child is really obedient; everyone likes him. He spends all day at home, doing work together with us. But this time, when I returned from the front line, alas, his mother and son were not at home; they had gone to play at their grandmother's house. Actually, it wasn't playing, to be honest. It was just to beg for a simple meal. Now, I don't know what happened to them. I originally wanted to see them, but because I was rushing to flee with everyone, I didn't even get to see them. Alas! It's pitiful that the child has suffered so much with his mother in this life... I really love him, but I'm afraid I won't see him on this journey.

(Everyone is moved by what he said. There is silence for a minute. Then, the medic suddenly wakes everyone up as if from a dream.)

Medic: It's clear that this retreat has harmed a lot of ordinary people. (At this time, the door and windows are slowly filled with people, sometimes even standing inside.) And we retreated so quickly. I'm a medic, following the army to rescue wounded soldiers. On the night of the twelfth, around one o'clock in the morning, we retreated from Luan City to Gubei. At two o'clock in the afternoon on the thirteenth, an order came from above to immediately transport heavy items to the rear. By eight o'clock in the evening, I thought I could finally get a good night's sleep, but another order came to move out immediately, requiring us to retreat to Xugezhuang. In two days and one night, it was almost three hundred li. So those ordinary people were naturally in a state of utter confusion. As soon as they heard that the army was retreating, they panicked immediately, like ants on a hot pot, only knowing to blindly follow the army and run around. Humph, this station is packed with people; I'm afraid there are countless people crying on the road.

Madam: (Slowly moves from over there to her own seat) That old man is really pitiful. Having to suffer like this at such an old age.

Maid: So what can we do?

Miss A: What can we do is what we just said.

Orderly: (Shouting from outside as he enters)

Go, go, go! What are you doing standing here? There's nothing to see here! Go!

(The crowd doesn't move at first, but then, seeing him take out his gun, they scatter in fear. At this time, Miss B sits alone in a chair, silent.)

Young Master: (Sitting and shouting) De Fa! Come here.

I want to talk to you. (The orderly goes over.)

Medic: Well then, I'll go now. Miss, you should still take him to Beiping for treatment. It's okay on the road; I've already bandaged him well. (Exits)

Young Master: You and the driver take that old fellow to the stationmaster and ask him to find a doctor to try to give him treatment. Here's twenty dollars for their medical expenses.

Miss B: (Rushes over) What? You're not willing to take him to Beiping for treatment? What does this mean!

Miss A: Look, here she comes again, going crazy again.

Miss B: I'm going crazy? You're the one who's going crazy. You injured him; aren't you even going to get him treatment?

Young Master: We are getting him treatment. Going to Beiping is treatment, and getting treatment here is treatment. Why isn't it treatment?

Miss B: Getting treatment here? How can you even say that? What hospitals are there here? Is twenty dollars enough to cover the medical expenses?

Who are you fooling? And he originally wanted to flee to Beiping, but now you're giving him treatment here and not allowing him to go. What does this mean?

Auntie: Second Miss, I don't think you need to get so angry. He's not someone you know. Why are you so concerned about him? If you really take him to Beiping,

Dad will scold you.

Miss B: What are you afraid of? We injured him and only gave him twenty dollars to be done with it. How can we live with our conscience?

Young Master: Ah, what conscience are you talking about? We should do it this way. It can't be wrong. What do you young girls know?
