Film Special

The Meaning of "Wilderness Films"

— Mi Er

Films that take "virgin land" or backward ethnic groups as their subject matter or background are generally called "wilderness films."

Everyone knows that European and American film circles (especially the United States) are very enthusiastic about the production of wilderness films. To understand the reason for this, we must first understand the meaning of wilderness films, so that we can know that all the crises of capitalism have begun. Commodity surpluses, falling prices, and all capitalist countries are caught in a frenzy of recession. The reason is that the market is shrinking, and the purchasing power of the people is rapidly decreasing due to excessive exploitation. At this time, they (capitalist countries) have already entered the highest form | imperialism. They know that to reduce this crisis, there is only one way: to have another shameless, thieving war to redistribute and compete for colonial markets. Because there will be no more "virgin lands" in the world. Their attempt is reflected in films:

First, the promotion of war films, beautifying war to incite the people's interest in war and organize the people's war consciousness.

Second, the production of wilderness films, introducing colonies to the people, exaggerating the wealth of the colonies as much as possible, and describing the stupidity of the "natives" as much as possible, even using shameless, arbitrary propaganda such as "only white people can rule Africa" or "ruling colonies is to civilize the natives" to order the "people" to dream of developing colonies.

This is the current active meaning of general wilderness films. The most important aspect of the passive side is that sensitive filmmakers intentionally or unintentionally feel their own decline, and at the same time, they have no way to save themselves. They have no choice but to have the illusions of "escaping emptiness" and "returning to nature." They long for "primitive" life, so "Jane" in "Tarzan the Ape Man" enters the mountains with "Tarzan."

As for China, everyone knows that it is the largest market in the world, the people's livelihood of all imperialist countries. To exaggerate a bit, their economic situation changes with the purchasing of the Chinese people. Didn't Roosevelt say publicly that to revive the world economy, it is necessary to increase the purchasing power of the Chinese people? But the purchasing power of the Chinese people is not only not increasing because of their constant exploitation, but also greatly decreasing. This not only worries the imperialists, but also worries their pawns and lackeys. So they wanted to develop backward ethnic groups within China. So film once again became the vanguard!

Here, I am sure someone will stand up and retort, "Should we not film about the Yao and Miao people?" No, filming about the Yao and Miao people is absolutely necessary, but we should never ignore their real lives and urgent needs (liberation movements, etc.), and fabricate what "love stories" or "unofficial histories," etc. Not long ago, didn't we see news in the newspapers about an uprising of 150,000 Yao people? Although the newspapers said they were "Yao bandits," we know that they were resisting because they were oppressed, which is certain. So, isn't such a great subject worthy of our filming? "Asia's Clouds" has already been placed before us. Anti-imperialism and anti-feudalism are the truly good films that take backward ethnic groups as their subject matter!

Film Reviews

Review of "Desperate"

— Ling He

After watching this film, I just want to write down some opinions in principle.

Since the loss of Northeast China, it has undoubtedly aroused the resentment of the general petty bourgeoisie in China. The majority of people, awakened to their own way out in the sound of artillery fire, because they realized the reason why China was being invaded, were organized and engaged in a thorough anti-imperialist movement, actively embarking on the road to national war. But on the other hand, the unawakened masses, although they hated the atrocities of the Japanese army and eagerly demanded the recovery of lost territory, often confined themselves to a narrow national concept, so all they could do was a patriotic movement. What they showed was, on the one hand, boycotting enemy goods and, on the other hand, sacrificing themselves for the country.

Now, these two concepts are constantly fighting. We can also see two different divisions in film works. Liu Chunshan's "Desperate" naturally belongs to the latter. We can see in this work that he is full of indignation. He pays attention to the unemployment problem. He knows that China's only way out is to resist with force. He hates the treacherous merchants who sell enemy goods, and he hates the cruel oppression of the rich, but his understanding is wrong. In his narrow concept, there are many illusions. For example, he thinks that a rich woman is willing to abandon her status and fall in love with a petty thug, and that only overseas Chinese are enthusiastic about donating money to support the volunteer army. Therefore, based on his conscientious patriotic advocacy, on the one hand, he boycotted enemy goods, and on the other hand, he vigorously promoted domestic goods. Here, we do not deny the fact of the enemy's economic aggression, but we believe that conscientious patriotism is by no means an effective method. Moreover, Chinese national capital can never grow under the iron hooves of the great powers, although the great powers also hope that China can move from feudalism to capitalism and contradictoryly support the development of Chinese capital in a very small range. Therefore, we hope that the author can recognize this major premise and not be confined to the concept of patriotism and be caught in the trap of the oppressors. Otherwise, the author will eventually have no way out, and even affect the audience to fall into a dead end.

As for the technical aspects, we don't need to point out every small mistake, and we can only correct some in principle.

First, the author does not understand the basic structure of comedy. So, if this is assumed to be a slapstick comedy, then it is a fundamental failure.

Second, in terms of content, this should be performed in a slapstick style.

Third, the protagonist should not be forcibly written as a hero.

In this way, its childish and vulgar achievements are naturally inevitable. Therefore, when we see that the treacherous merchant has a bizarre eye-rolling disease, which is cured with one medicine, and that Japanese Ajinomoto is used to treat hemorrhoids, etc., we can't help but sigh. Other things, such as the illegality of Montage and all the impure techniques, are all things that we hope the author will work harder on.

So our conclusion is: "The activism of the petty bourgeoisie is fully expressed in this film, but the performance is too disappointing."

Wastepaper Basket

— Bu Min

It is certainly unfortunate for manuscripts to go into the wastepaper basket, but as for the editors, there will never be an act of "disregarding life." This is a statement that the editors want to make to the readers and writers who care about this publication. Manuscripts with incoherent language, lack of substance, and excessive publicity are in danger of being thrown into the wastepaper basket at any time. As for usable manuscripts that cannot be published due to a lack of space, apart from those that are attached with self-addressed stamped envelopes that are returned at any time, they also have to be placed on the desk, waiting for the opportunity to be published. But if the timeliness is lost, they can only go into the wastepaper basket. Today, two manuscripts have also suffered the fate of being thrown into the wastepaper basket: one is Yi Hua's correspondence, concerning the filming of an airplane film in Hangzhou, a clearly usable manuscript, but a publicity department's blue-black stamp of more than two square inches was stamped in the middle of the text. Many words could not be seen. It was impossible to revise, and it was impossible to typeset. It's like an employee in the post office, clearly a scenic postcard sent from overseas, who stamps the postmark on the picture (spoiling the scenery) instead of stamping it elsewhere. Clearly, there is a lot of empty space on the back of the manuscript, but they don't stamp there and want to stamp on the words. It equally represents the bad habit of not cherishing things in China, so I decided not to use it and threw it into the wastepaper basket. Probably readers will not see my method as arbitrary. There is also a manuscript from Ge Zhuo, concerning the Yue Ming Film Company's "Bad Neighbor." This is a manuscript written by Ge Zhuo after watching the screening of "Bad Neighbor." Because there are many malpractices in publishing all kinds of previews, announcements, and introductions, I must wait until a film is publicly released and get an accurate review, and then consider publishing some audience opinions. I think this is a fair method, so Ge Zhuo's manuscript also went into the wastepaper basket. Yesterday, there were also several manuscripts, one written horizontally in the style of crab writing, one written on both sides, and one written in pencil, all of which were thrown into the wastepaper basket. Chinese characters are traditionally written from right to left, from top to bottom. Horizontal writing or writing on both sides is detrimental to typesetting work, so they are all rejected. As for pencil writing, once it reaches the inky hands of the typesetters, it becomes a mess, unable to distinguish black from white. I think it's better to keep some black and white.

Audience Opinions

— Bu Min

Editor's Note: "Golden Mountain" is a foreign film, but it is not produced by "a country that takes the money we pay for films that insult our Chinese nation." Moreover, it has many lessons for us. What I have heard from people's mouths are all good comments, so I broke the rule and revealed some of the audience's opinions.

Talking about "Golden Mountain"

— Yao Yinzong

Undoubtedly, the new Soviet film "Golden Mountain," which is currently being screened, is the same as "Raw Road" in that it is an expression of "force," and the "force" of "Golden Mountain" is even stronger than that of "Raw Road." Like "Raw Road," it lacks soft seductiveness; all it has is strong excitement. It is impossible to satisfy the young masters of the leisure class; it can only give them a boring and dull feeling!

Its structural form is similar to "Asia's Clouds" in that both have "resistance" as their central idea: the difference is in the content. "Asia's Clouds" takes "nation" as its position, while "Golden Mountain" takes "class" as its position; the target of "Asia's Clouds" is "imperialism," while the target of "Golden Mountain" is "the bourgeoisie."

"Golden Mountain" exposes the greed, tyranny, and deception of the oppressed class | the bourgeoisie toward the oppressed class | the proletariat very vividly.

As for the performance, it is certainly very successful. Each actor is not a novice in film techniques, especially the two actors who played the worker Peter and the foreman, who have great attainments in film techniques. The pitiful coolie and the foreman who is loyal to the factory owner but insidious and cunning to the workers are both portrayed vividly thanks to the efforts of these two actors. The director's technique is very flexible, and he has put a lot of effort into the arrangement of the scenes. There are several places in it that are not found in the films of other capitalist countries, which can be regarded as the creation of the Soviet film industry.

Kissing on the Silver Screen

— Dong Lin

Young people who have watched foreign films think that foreign stars can hug beautiful women and kiss them, and that they are so lucky! In fact, they don't know the illusion of it!

Everyone knows that Clark Gable has kissed many times on the screen! But when you hear about his painful experience with kissing, you can't help but be surprised.

He said: "Up to now, I have filmed kissing scenes with more than fifty actresses. But these are all just fake! If you don't believe me, although you are hugging and kissing in the film studio, you are strangers with no relationship once you leave the film studio! I don't know if it's because the director doesn't allow me to, but I probably slip away when my lips are a third of an inch close, but this requires a lot of hard practice to make it look real. But if you use a microscope to magnify it hundreds of times, then it's not right. To be honest, only the stars know!"

Movie Novels

Full River Red (V)

— Qian Bai

Oh Heavens! Erxiang was only Xinye's lover; he was merely painting a portrait for her. How could it inexplicably ruin the love between him and Taozhi! Yet, she indirectly bought the painting and endured the pain of marrying Youguang. How great was her painstaking effort, her sacrifice! Her small heart will forever bear this indelible scar; how heartbroken she must be! Decided, Shuicun decided to rush to Shanghai to explain to her. He had misunderstood her before, and she came to explain to him time and time again. Now that she has misunderstood him, how could he not go and explain? But in this vast Shanghai, where could he find the tiny Taozhi? Taozhi and Youguang held their wedding. Although he saw it, he didn't have the courage to rush up and explain to Taozhi. He really didn't know what to do. Suddenly, a well-dressed middle-aged woman, leading two children, squeezed through the crowd into the auditorium and pointed at Youguang, saying angrily, "Good! You dare to get married again? What about me and the children?" This was truly a killjoy, but Youguang obediently followed the woman and children away. How heartbroken was Taozhi after this terrible change? Besides crying, what else could she do? Shuicun felt very sympathetic and sorrowful for her, but he was unwilling to miss this opportunity to explain. Shuicun explained to her; Taozhi accepted his explanation. Shuicun also told her that he was going to Hankou.

"Why do you suddenly want to go to Hankou?"

"Because in these few days, I have realized that 'love' is a game played by people with money and leisure. We poor fellows should transfer the passion and energy of love to the environment where the powerful cannot eat, and struggle for our own livelihoods!" "…"

Taozhi had a deep understanding of Shuicun, so before Shuicun left, she felt that she should at least see Shuicun once and talk to him again. But when she rushed to the ship, Shuicun was already dead drunk. The ship was about to depart, but under such circumstances, how could Taozhi be willing to go ashore alone and leave Shuicun to go away drunk?

"Fire! Fire!"

In the dead of night, suddenly, people became noisy. Men and women, old and young, rushed to the deck one after another, scrambling to be the first. Why? Ah! It turned out that the cargo ship had been careless, and the fire was already out of control. Taozhi called out to Shuicun, but he did not wake up for a long time. How could Taozhi abandon Shuicun and run away alone? This really worried Taozhi! In an instant, the red light filled the river surface. It seemed that neither Shuicun nor Taozhi had escaped the encirclement of the red light. (The End)
